## Phase A — Cluster Review: C17

[PHASE-A] C17 | 2026-04-10

### Cluster identity
C17 groups ten registries under the broad domain of relational inner-being characteristics. The cluster's working title is "relational/covenantal affection" — a provisional label drawn from the dominant vocabulary: love, mercy, compassion, kindness, grace, forgiveness, fellowship, covenant, peace, reconciliation.

### Excluded registries (Analysis Complete — no further processing)
- Reg 68 (grace) — 11 groups excluded from Phase B/C/coverage

### Active registries and group counts

| Registry | Word | Total groups | Source list |
|---|---|---|---|
| 23 | compassion | 22 | High Confidence |
| 34 | covenant | 32 | Missing Inner Being Words |
| 62 | fellowship | 4 | Missing Inner Being Words |
| 64 | forgiveness | 14 | High Confidence |
| 99 | kindness | 28 | Missing Inner Being Words |
| 103 | love | 66 | High Confidence |
| 111 | mercy | 36 | Missing Inner Being Words |
| 117 | peace | 69 | Missing Inner Being Words |
| 130 | reconciliation | 2 | Missing Inner Being Words |

Active group total: 284 − 11 (Reg 68) = **273 active groups** requiring Phase B.

### Coherence assessment

**What holds this cluster together:**

The dominant inner-being affinity across the active registries is *relational disposition* — the orientation of an inner person (whether divine or human) toward another. Compassion (23), love (103), mercy (111), kindness (99), fellowship (62), forgiveness (64), and reconciliation (130) all name inner states or movements oriented toward another. Grace (68, excluded) belongs here by the same logic.

Covenant (34) and peace (117) are the most complex registries in coherence terms:

- **Covenant (34)**: The word `berit` and its associated vocabulary (oath, cutting, ark) are primarily structural — they name the relational framework, not the inner disposition within it. However, the verse evidence shows that covenant language consistently evokes inner-being states: commitment, loyalty, transformation (new covenant/heart), moral consequence, and communal identity. The cluster assignment is coherent insofar as covenant *names the structure* within which the relational inner-being characteristics of this cluster operate. Covenant is the relational bond; love, mercy, compassion, and kindness are its inner character. This relationship is analytically significant and will need careful Phase C treatment: some covenant groups may belong more naturally to Transformation (Dimension 08) or Moral Character (Dimension 05) than to relational disposition categories.

- **Peace (117)**: This is the largest active registry (69 groups) and has the most heterogeneous dimension spread in the automated labels: Dependence/Creatureliness, Divine-Human Correspondence, Emotion (Positive and Negative), Cognition, Volition, Agency/Power, Moral Character, Relational Disposition, Vitality/Existence — and 12 UNCLASSIFIED groups. The Hebrew shalom family (rest, quiet, silence, stillness terms) pulls strongly toward Emotion and Dependence rather than Relational Disposition. Many of the silence/rest terms (da.mam, cha.resh, sha.qat, nu.ach) may describe inner states or conditions rather than relational orientations. Peace as "relational restoration" (eirēnē — Reg 130 connection) is coherent with the cluster; peace as "inner stillness/rest" is borderline. This is the primary boundary question for C17. Phase B and C will need to work carefully through the silence/rest/stillness vocabulary to determine whether it belongs in C17 or should be proposed for reassignment.

- **Reconciliation (130)**: Very small (2 groups), both KEYWORD_STRONG with Divine-Human Correspondence. Coherence is strong — both groups name the restoration of the broken divine-human relational bond. The smallness is not a concern given the focused vocabulary.

- **Kindness (99)**: This registry has an unusual cluster of terms that do not obviously belong to kindness as an inner-being characteristic: H5971 (am — people), H5973 (me.im — from/with), H5974 (im — with/among), H2098 (zu — this/which), H2090 (zoh — this), H1668 (da — this), H2097 (zo — this), H0120G (a.dam — humanity/person). These are particles, pronouns, and generic human terms. Their presence in Reg 99 (kindness) requires Phase B attention. They appear to have been assigned here from the "Missing Inner Being Words" source list — their inner-being content, if any, will need careful assessment. Some may be thin or borderline; others may carry genuine inner-being content in specific verse contexts (e.g. am as "covenant people" carrying communal inner identity). This is a quality observation, not a reassignment proposal at this stage.

**Boundary observations:**

1. **Peace (117) — silence/rest/stillness terms**: Multiple terms in Reg 117 describe inner quiet, rest, and stillness (sha.qat, nu.ach, da.mam, cha.resh, cha.shah, and related terms). If their groups primarily name an inner condition of rest or emotional stillness rather than a relational orientation, they may sit more naturally in Emotion — Positive (Dimension 01), Dependence/Creatureliness (Dimension 10), or possibly a distinct "rest/stillness" category. This is a Phase B/C question, not a Phase A conclusion.

2. **Covenant (34) — ritual/structural terms**: Groups 3270-001 (kibōtos — ark), 3271-001 (kibōtos — ark), 765-003/766-002 (new covenant/heart transformation) and 777-series (kainos — newness) may belong more to Transformation (Dimension 08) than to Relational Disposition. These are legitimate Phase C discernment questions.

3. **Kindness (99) — particle/pronoun terms**: As noted above, the presence of structural/grammatical terms in Reg 99 is unexpected and requires Phase B scrutiny. This is not a cluster reassignment issue — it is a registry quality question.

4. **Mercy (111) — atonement vocabulary**: Reg 111 carries significant atonement/propitiation vocabulary (kip.per, kap.po.ret, hilasmos, hilaskomai). This vocabulary connects directly to Reg 64 (forgiveness) and to Relational Disposition more broadly. The cluster assignment is coherent — atonement is the mechanism by which mercy is enacted relationally — but the dimension assignment in Phase C will need to distinguish between the *inner character* of mercy (Relational Disposition), the *act of covering/atoning* (which may be Agency/Power or a distinct sub-type), and the *inner state of the supplicant* (Dependence/Creatureliness or Emotion — Negative).

### Cross-registry root families

Five cross-registry root families identified in the root family extract. All five span C17 and other clusters:

| Root | Terms in C17 | Registries in C17 | Registers outside C17 |
|---|---|---|---|
| CHASAD | H2616A, H2617B (Reg 23) | 23 | Reg 146 (shame — H2616B cha.sad) |
| TOV | H2895 (Reg 103) | 103 | Reg 67 (goodness — H2896A tov) |
| AGAV | H5691 (Reg 103) | 103 | Reg 43 (desire — H5690 a.gav) |
| EL | H1180, H5251H, H7067G, H0410G (Reg 117) | 117 | Reg 13 (bitterness — H0413 el), Reg 196 (power — H0410G el) |
| DAM | H1748, H1820, H1826A, H1826H, H1827 (Reg 117) | 117 | Reg 116 (patience — H1826 da.mam) |

**Notable cross-registry observations:**

- **CHASAD root (Reg 23 / Reg 146)**: H2616A (cha.sad — be kind) and H2617B (che.sed — shame/steadfast love) are in Reg 23 (compassion). H2616B (cha.sad — to shame) is in Reg 146 (shame). The CHASAD root spans two opposite ends of relational experience: covenantal love/kindness and shame. This is a potential Session D pointer — the same root covering both the relational bond and its violation. Note also that H2617B is glossed "shame" in the root family extract but its groups in the cluster (1633-001, 1633-002, 1633-003) describe *steadfast love/chesed*, not shame. This gloss inconsistency requires Phase B attention.

- **DAM root (Reg 117 / Reg 116)**: The silence/stillness root spans peace (117) and patience (116). This cross-registry root resonance confirms that the silence/stillness vocabulary in Reg 117 has lexical kinship with patience/endurance — a finding relevant to Phase C dimension assignment for the dam.am/du.mam/de.ma.mah groups.

- **EL root (Reg 117)**: The EL root cluster in Reg 117 includes ba.a.li (Baal/God), nes (ensign/banner), qan.na (Jealous God), and el (God/towards) — terms that span theological naming and directional prepositions. Their presence in Reg 117 (peace) reflects verse-context assignment decisions made during the Verse Context stage; Phase B will need to assess whether the inner-being content of their groups justifies their placement here.

### Recommendation

CONFIRM C17 cluster assignment as-is. The cluster holds genuine inner-being affinity around relational disposition, covenantal character, and relational restoration.

**Flags for Phase B attention (not reassignment proposals — quality and discernment questions):**
1. Reg 99 (kindness) — particle/pronoun/generic-human terms require Phase B quality scrutiny
2. Reg 117 (peace) — silence/rest/stillness vocabulary: Phase B/C must determine whether groups name relational orientation or inner condition
3. H2617B gloss inconsistency (Reg 23) — "shame" gloss but groups describe steadfast love/chesed: flag for Phase B
4. Reg 34 (covenant) — structural/ritual groups may dimension-assign outside relational categories: Phase C discernment required

**Size note:** C17 is very large — 273 active groups across 9 registries. Reg 117 (69 groups) and Reg 103 (66 groups) alone account for nearly half the cluster. Per Section 6.1 and 6.6, Phase B for C17 must be split across multiple sessions. Recommended split: Reg 23/34/62/64 (72 groups) as one session; Reg 99/103 (94 groups) as one session; Reg 111/117/130 (107 groups) as one session.

### Reg 23 — compassion (22 groups)

[PHASE-B] 1616-001 | H7362 ra.cha.ma.ni | Reg 23 (compassion)
QA-FLAG: QA-CLEAR
Note: Description names the inner quality of compassion as a human characteristic and notes its violation under catastrophe. Characteristic-perspective model applied correctly — the term names the quality, not just the action. Sufficient for dimension assignment.

[PHASE-B] 1633-001 | H2617B che.sed | Reg 23 (compassion)
QA-FLAG: QA-REVIEW
Note: The root family extract glosses H2617B as "shame," but this group's description names God's steadfast love/chesed as his covenantal inner disposition. The anchor verses (Exo 34:6; Lam 3:22) unambiguously describe steadfast love, not shame. This is either a STEP gloss disambiguation issue (H2617A vs H2617B assigned differently) or a root extract data error. The group description itself is clear and sufficient for dimension assignment. The gloss anomaly does not affect the group content. Flag for Claude Code to verify H2617B gloss in the STEP database. No description correction required.

[PHASE-B] 1633-002 | H2617B che.sed | Reg 23 (compassion)
QA-FLAG: QA-REVIEW
Note: Same H2617B gloss anomaly as 1633-001. Description correctly names human covenantal loyalty/loving-kindness. Anchor verses (Hos 6:6; Mic 6:8) support. Sufficient for dimension assignment. Same gloss verification flag applies.

[PHASE-B] 1633-003 | H2617B che.sed | Reg 23 (compassion)
QA-FLAG: QA-REVIEW
Note: Same H2617B gloss anomaly. Description names the human appeal to God's chesed as a sustaining inner orientation. Anchor verses (Psa 25:7; Psa 48:9) support. Sufficient for dimension assignment. Same flag applies.

### Reg 34 — covenant (32 groups)

[PHASE-B] 3270-001 | G2787G kibōtos | Reg 34 (covenant)
QA-FLAG: QA-TERMCENTRIC
Note: Description reads "The ark as the visible sign of God's covenant presence and faithfulness." This names what the term (ark) represents externally rather than the inner-being characteristic the verse cluster engages. The anchor (Rev 11:19 — the ark seen in the opened temple amid lightning and earthquake) shows a theophanic moment of awe and cosmic judgment. The inner-being characteristic engaged is not named. Phase B.5 required.

[PHASE-B5] 3270-001 | REWRITE
OLD: The ark as the visible sign of God's covenant presence and faithfulness
NEW: Reverential awe before the holy — the ark as the mediating sign that orients the inner person toward the presence and faithfulness of God
RATIONALE: The description named the external object (ark) and what it signifies externally. The anchor verse (Rev 11:19) situates the ark's appearance in a theophanic context of lightning, thunder, earthquake — overwhelming divine presence. The inner-being characteristic engaged is the human response of awe and orientation toward the holy, mediated through the covenant sign. The term serves as the mediating vehicle; the characteristic is the inner stance of reverence and trust before God's covenant faithfulness.
PATCH-TARGET: verse_context_group.id = 464 | wa_dimension_index.id = 6654

[PHASE-B] 3271-001 | G2787H kibōtos | Reg 34 (covenant)
QA-FLAG: QA-TERMCENTRIC
Note: Description reads "The ark as means of preservation amid judgment — framing inner-being contrast of obedience and heedlessness." Names the ark's narrative function (means of preservation) rather than the inner-being characteristic. Anchor (1Pe 3:20 — "a few, eight persons, were brought safely through water") grounds the contrast of those who did and did not enter. Phase B.5 required.

[PHASE-B5] 3271-001 | REWRITE
OLD: The ark as means of preservation amid judgment — framing inner-being contrast of obedience and heedlessness
NEW: Obedience under judgment — the ark as the instrument that separates the inner orientation of faithful response from heedless disregard
RATIONALE: The old description named the ark's role as means of preservation but did not name the inner characteristic. The anchor verse (1Pe 3:20) draws attention to those "who formerly did not obey" — the inner orientation of disobedience is what the verse foregrounds as the contrast. The characteristic engaged is obedience/heedlessness as inner orientation, with the ark as the instrument that makes the contrast visible.
PATCH-TARGET: verse_context_group.id = 465 | wa_dimension_index.id = 6655

[PHASE-B] 3314-001 | H7620I sha.vu.a | Reg 34 (covenant)
QA-FLAG: QA-VAGUE
Note: Description reads "Prophetic weeks as the divinely appointed schedule for covenant fulfillment." This names the temporal unit and its function (schedule) but does not name the inner-being characteristic engaged. The anchor (Dan 9:24 — "seventy weeks are decreed about your people...to finish the transgression, to put an end to sin, to atone for iniquity, to bring in everlasting righteousness") contains significant inner-being content (transgression, sin, iniquity, righteousness, atonement). The description misses this content entirely. The group may belong more to Transformation or Moral Character once the inner-being characteristic is identified from the verse. Correction proposed.

PROPOSED CORRECTION for 3314-001: "Divine appointment for inner-being completion — the seventy weeks marking the decreed period for the end of sin, atonement for iniquity, and the arrival of everlasting righteousness"
RATIONALE: The verse (Dan 9:24) makes explicit that the weeks frame a programme of inner-being transformation: sin ended, iniquity atoned, righteousness established. The inner characteristic is the trajectory of moral-spiritual completion, not merely the temporal schedule.

[PHASE-B5] 767-001 | REWRITE
OLD: The covenantal cutting ritual — self-imprecatory act underlying oath
NEW: Inner commitment under solemn self-curse — the cutting ritual as the enactment of the will's binding to covenant terms, with transgression named as the inner failure it judges
RATIONALE: The description named the ritual (cutting) and its structural role (self-imprecatory) without naming the inner characteristic. The anchor verse (Jer 34:18) focuses on those who transgressed — the inner moral failure is what the ritual's self-curse was meant to prevent. The inner characteristic is the solemn binding of the will under covenant terms, and its violation.

Anchor (Psa 130:4 — "with you there is forgiveness, that you may be feared") shows forgiveness producing fear/reverence — an inner-being response to divine character. The Emotion — Negative label appears to have been triggered by the word "fear" rather than the group's actual content, which is about divine character and the human response of reverence. Phase C must correct. The description itself is adequate. Clear for Phase B.

### Reg 99 — kindness (28 groups)

[PHASE-B] 5729-001 | G5541 chrēsteuomai | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-CLEAR
Note: Description names kindness as the inner quality of love — the outward expression of love's inner character toward others. Anchor (1Cor 13:4 — "love is patient and kind") grounds kindness as an attribute of love's inner character. Clear.

[PHASE-B] 5730-001 | G5542 chrēstologia | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-CLEAR
Note: Description names the deceptive inner disposition expressed as flattering speech — false kindness targeting the naive. Anchor (Rom 16:18 — "by smooth talk and flattery they deceive the hearts of the naive") grounds this in inner deception expressed outwardly. The group captures the counterfeit of kindness as an inner-being phenomenon. Clear.

[PHASE-B] 5731-001 | H5973B me.im | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-REVIEW
Note: H5973B me.im is a preposition meaning "from with/away from." Its presence in Reg 99 (kindness) is unexpected — this is a preposition, not a kindness term. The description ("Departure from relational presence expressing inner relational states — grief at loss, guilt, inner fear of separation") captures genuine inner-being content from the anchor verses (Gen 44:29; Gen 44:32 — Jacob's grief at the potential loss of Benjamin). However, the connection to "kindness" is indirect — the term signals departure from relational presence, which only registers as inner-being content because of the surrounding verse narrative. This is a property-term group. The description is adequate for dimension assignment. The cluster assignment (Reg 99) is unusual for a preposition but not wrong if the verse evidence supports inner-being content. Flag for information; no description correction required.

[PHASE-B] 5732-001 | H5971K am | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-CLEAR
Note: Description names military force as communal subject of inner responses to battle — fear, courage, trust in God. Anchors (Deu 20:1; Jos 8:1) both address inner orientation ("do not fear," "do not be dismayed"). H5971K is a distinct form of am (people) used in military contexts. The description identifies the communal inner response as the characteristic. Clear.

[PHASE-B] 5733-001 | H5971B am | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-CLEAR
Note: Description names relational community of belonging — gathered to or cut off from one's people as inner belonging, covenant faithfulness, or moral transgression. Anchors (Gen 25:8 — "gathered to his people"; Lev 17:10 — "cut off from among his people") ground the inner-belonging dimension. Clear.

[PHASE-B] 5735-001 | H5974 im | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-REVIEW
Note: H5974 im is a preposition meaning "with." Description names relational presence of God or companions as the context for inner experience. Anchors (Dan 2:18 — seeking mercy from God; Dan 4:34 — Nebuchadnezzar's reason returning) show genuine inner content dependent on the "with" relationship. As with 5731-001, this is a property-term group where the preposition serves as an inner-being context marker. Description is adequate. Flag for information; no description correction required. Note for Phase C: dimension assignment will need to focus on the inner-being characteristic contextualised by the presence, not on the preposition itself.

[PHASE-B] 5737-001 | H5971H am | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-BROAD
Note: Description reads "Covenant community as object of God's relational love and moral claim — 'my people' as relational partner of the divine." However, anchors (Num 11:29 — Moses wishing all the Lord's people were prophets; Num 14:19 — Moses interceding for the people's iniquity) show two different inner-being characteristics: (1) the prophetic gift given to the people (11:29) and (2) intercession for pardon based on God's steadfast love (14:19). The single description conflates these. However, the group's anchor verses both use the same term in similar contexts (Moses speaking about/for "the people"), so the grouping may be intentional as a Moses-intercessor context. The description focuses only on God's relational claim and does not name the inner-being content of either verse adequately. Correction proposed.

PROPOSED CORRECTION for 5737-001: "The covenant people as the object of divine care and human intercession — Moses's inner orientation of solidarity and advocacy for Israel grounded in God's steadfast love"
RATIONALE: Both anchors show Moses in intercessory solidarity with the people — the inner characteristic is his advocacy/intercession oriented toward both God and people. The description's focus on God's relational claim misses the intercessory human inner-being content.
Researcher decision required before patch.

[PHASE-B] 5737-002 | H5971H am | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-CLEAR
Note: Description names the corporate inner spiritual condition of the people — rebellion, fear, trust, shame. Anchors (Num 14:9 — "do not rebel...do not fear"; Num 14:11 — "how long will this people despise me") support. Both verses name inner-being states of the people collectively. Clear.

[PHASE-B] 5737-003 | H5971H am | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-VAGUE
Note: Description reads "People as bearer of communal inner identity — shared moral-spiritual character defining who 'the people' are." The anchor (Exo 7:14 — "Pharaoh's heart is hardened; he refuses to let the people go") does not obviously demonstrate communal inner identity. The verse is about Pharaoh's inner state (hardened heart, refusal), not about the people's identity. The description does not match the anchor verse.

PROPOSED CORRECTION for 5737-003: "The people as the object of God's liberating purpose — their situation as the ground of divine action, with Pharaoh's hardened refusal as the inner obstacle"
RATIONALE: Exo 7:14 is about Pharaoh's inner state (hardened heart) in relation to the people. The inner-being content is Pharaoh's refusal/hardness. The description's claim about "communal inner identity" is not grounded in this anchor verse. The group may need a vertical pass extract if other verses in the group do show communal identity — but from this anchor alone, the description is unsupported.
Researcher decision required — confirm proposed correction or request vertical pass for this group.

INSTRUCTION-NOTE for Reg 99 am-variants: H5971B, H5971H, H5971I, H5971L appear to be STEP disambiguation variants of the same root term am (people). Groups 5737-001/5738-001/5739-001 share identical descriptions and anchor verses; same for the -002 and -003 subgroups. This is likely an artefact of STEP's multi-form tagging for the same lexeme. Session B for Reg 99 should examine whether these variants carry meaningfully distinct verse evidence or whether the grouping structure is partially redundant. Flag for Session B.

[PHASE-B] 5769-001 | H2098 zu | Reg 99 (kindness)
QA-FLAG: QA-TERMCENTRIC
Note: Description reads "Term connects and qualifies inner-being content — directing attention to persons or conditions where inner life is expressed." This is a property-term description naming what the particle does (connects, directs attention) without naming the inner-being characteristic. Anchors (Psa 142:3 — "when my spirit faints within me, you know my way"; Psa 143:8 — "let me hear in the morning of your steadfast love, for in you I trust") show rich inner content: spiritual faintness, trust, dependence. Phase B.5 required.

[PHASE-B5] 5769-001 | REWRITE
OLD: Term connects and qualifies inner-being content — directing attention to persons or conditions where inner life is expressed
NEW: Spiritual faintness and trust — the inner person in extremity, directing its cry and its trust toward God as the one who knows the way
RATIONALE: The particle zu/this in the anchor verses points to the inner condition of the person: faint spirit (Psa 142:3) and the trust-and-longing posture of Psa 143:8. The description named only the grammatical function; the anchors show a specific inner-being cluster of faintness, dependence, and directed trust. The characteristic is the inner person's orientation in extremity.
PATCH-TARGET: verse_context_group.id = 1478 | wa_dimension_index.id = 7671

[PHASE-B] 990-001 | H5750 od | Reg 111 (mercy)

Phase B.5 required.

[PHASE-B5] 990-001 | REWRITE
OLD: Term intensifies or marks the persistence/cessation of a human inner-being state — amplifying the force of an inner disposition or qualifying the duration of inner orientation
NEW: Persistence and turning — the duration of inner moral orientation, whether integrity maintained under affliction or stubbornness that must cease
RATIONALE: The particle od marks the ongoing or ceasing character of inner states. The anchors show: Job still holding integrity under Satanic pressure (perseverance), and Israel's stubbornness destined to end in the new age (turning from evil inclination). The characteristic is the duration-dimension of inner moral orientation — its persistence or its necessary end.
PATCH-TARGET: verse_context_group.id = 1668 | wa_dimension_index.id = 7847

[PHASE-B] 2589-001 | H2010 ha.na.chah | Reg 117 (peace)
QA-FLAG: QA-VAGUE
Note: Description reads "Term names the granting of relief — a remission that brings rest and lightening of burden to those who receive it." The description names the act (granting of relief) without naming the inner-being characteristic of the recipient. Anchor (Est 2:18 — Artaxerxes granting a remission of taxes at Esther's feast) is about a governmental act, not primarily an inner-being experience. The inner-being content of this group is unclear from the description.

PROPOSED CORRECTION for 2589-001: "Relief from burden — the inner experience of rest and ease when pressure is lifted, as the condition of those who receive remission or royal favour"
RATIONALE: The description names what is granted (relief) but not what is experienced inwardly. The inner characteristic is the condition of the recipient — ease, lightening of burden. The anchor is thin and the inner content indirect; a vertical pass extract would confirm whether other verses in the group show richer inner-being content.
Researcher decision required — confirm proposed correction or request vertical pass.

[PHASE-B] 415-001 | H1585 ge.mar | Reg 117 (peace)
QA-FLAG: QA-TERMCENTRIC
Note: Description reads "Term names the formal salutation of peace — the invocation of wholeness and wellbeing at the opening of official correspondence." This names the function of the formula (salutation, invocation) without naming the inner-being characteristic the salutation expresses or effects. Anchor (Ezr 7:12 — Artaxerxes's letter opening "Peace") is a diplomatic formula. Phase B.5 assessment: the inner-being content of a formal peace salutation is the inner orientation of goodwill and well-wishing extended toward the recipient. The characteristic is present even if thin in this single-verse anchor.

[PHASE-B5] 415-001 | REWRITE
OLD: Term names the formal salutation of peace — the invocation of wholeness and wellbeing at the opening of official correspondence
NEW: Wellbeing expressed in greeting — the inner orientation of goodwill and wholeness directed toward another through formal invocation of peace
RATIONALE: The description named the formula (salutation, correspondence) rather than the inner-being characteristic the formula conveys. The characteristic is the goodwill/wellbeing orientation extended toward another — the inner reality the salutation both names and enacts.
PATCH-TARGET: verse_context_group.id = 1724 | wa_dimension_index.id = 7894

## Phase C — Dimension Discernment: Reg 23 (compassion)

Session 5. Resuming from SESSION-END marker (Phase B complete, coverage 273/273 confirmed). Phase C begins for Reg 23 — 22 groups.

  Session B: next = DIM-23-001
  Session D: next = DIM-23-SD001

[PHASE-C] 1616-001 | H7362 ra.cha.ma.ni | Reg 23 (compassion)
Term type: Characteristic term — names the inner quality directly
DESC (confirmed): Term names the inner quality of compassion as a defining human characteristic — its violation by circumstances of extreme suffering marking the depth of the catastrophe

AV-VERIFY 1616-001 | Lam 4:10
AV: Lam 4:10 — "The hands of compassionate women have boiled their own children; they became their food during the destruction of the daughter of my people."
DESC covers: The inner quality of compassion as a defining human characteristic; its violation under extremity.
VERSE also shows: The extremity is so profound that the compassionate quality itself collapses — the verse does not merely name an absence of compassion but names the women by their compassionate character and then shows that character overwhelmed. The catastrophe is measured by the inner quality it destroys.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Relational Disposition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: Compassion here is a stable inner character quality of the human person — the disposition of tender regard toward vulnerable others. The verse reveals the quality by its negation under catastrophe. Automated label Relational Disposition is correct. Toward-another orientation confirmed.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 6539

---

[PHASE-C] 1633-001 | H2617B che.sed | Reg 23 (compassion)
Term type: Characteristic term (chesed names the quality directly)
DESC (confirmed, QA-REVIEW gloss anomaly noted): Term names God's steadfast love as the defining inner character of his covenantal disposition toward his people — the loyal, enduring, freely given love that grounds all relationship with him
Note: H2617B gloss in root extract reads "shame" but all group content describes chesed/steadfast love. Proceeding on the basis of the group description and anchor verse content.

AV-VERIFY 1633-001 | Exo 34:6
AV: Exo 34:6 — "The Lord, the Lord, a God merciful and gracious, slow to anger, and abounding in steadfast love and faithfulness."
DESC covers: God's steadfast love as the defining inner character of his covenantal disposition — loyal, enduring, freely given.
VERSE also shows: Chesed here is part of the Sinai theophanic self-declaration — paired with mercy, graciousness, patience, and faithfulness. The verse grounds chesed as a divine inner attribute in the foundational moment of covenant renewal. The fullness of the character portrait exceeds chesed alone but the group is correctly anchored here.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 1633-001 | Lam 3:22
AV: Lam 3:22 — "The steadfast love of the Lord never ceases; his mercies never come to an end."
DESC covers: The loyal, enduring, freely given love — "never ceases" confirms the enduring quality.
VERSE also shows: The never-ceasing quality is paired with mercies (plural) — both speak to God's sustained inner disposition. No gap.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Relational Disposition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: GOD
NOTES: Chesed as divine steadfast love is the paradigmatic Relational Disposition — God's settled, enduring inner orientation of covenantal love toward his people. [SESSION-D] DIM-23-SD001
REGISTRY: 23 (compassion)
SESSION-TARGET: D
DESCRIPTION: The Hebrew root CHASAD (Reg 23) crosses into Reg 146 (shame): H2616A cha.sad (be kind) and H2617B che.sed (steadfast love) are in Reg 23; H2616B cha.sad (to shame) is in Reg 146. The same root family spans the two poles of relational experience: covenantal love/mercy (chus, chesed) and shame/exposure. This is not incidental — the same etymological root covers both the relational bond at its most loyal and the relational wound at its most exposed. Session D should examine whether this root-family crossing reveals a structural relationship between mercy and shame in the inner-being vocabulary of Scripture: whether the depth of mercy presupposes the depth of shame, or whether the vocabulary itself encodes the relational restoration movement (from shame/exposure to mercy/covering). Relevant registries: C17 (compassion/love/kindness/mercy) and C06 or equivalent shame cluster.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_session_research_flags insert

PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 6527

[PHASE-C] 733-001 | H5150 ni.chum | Reg 23 (compassion)
Term type: Characteristic term
DESC (confirmed): Term names the compassionate inner movement of comfort — the tender, stirring compassion that arises from within the person toward those who grieve or suffer

AV-VERIFY 733-001 | Isa 57:18
AV: Isa 57:18 — "I have seen his ways, but I will heal him; I will lead him and restore comfort to him and his mourners."
DESC covers: The compassionate inner movement of comfort — God's tender compassion expressed as healing, leading, and restoring comfort.
VERSE also shows: God acts despite "seeing his ways" — the compassion is not contingent on the person's deserving. The comfort is given to both the person and the mourners around him — communal restoration.

DESC covers: Tender, stirring compassion that arises from within — "my heart recoils within me; my compassion grows warm and tender" is perhaps the most explicit inner-being description of divine compassion in the Hebrew Bible.
VERSE also shows: The compassion is described as a physical inner stirring — "heart recoils," "grows warm and tender." The divine inner life is named with visceral intimacy. This is an inner experience of God, not merely a declaration.

[SESSION-B] DIM-23-001

The question for Session B is whether the compassion vocabulary of Reg 23 contains a sub-pattern of "visceral inner movement" terms (splanchnizō, ni.chum, ra.cha.mim) that share a somatic/embodied description of the inner compassion movement, and whether this sub-pattern spans the divine-human boundary (both God and humans described as "moved within" by compassion).

[PHASE-C] 734-001 | G4834 sumpatheō | Reg 23 (compassion)
Term type: Characteristic term (capacity and disposition for fellow-feeling)

The "yet without sin" qualification means the solidarity is genuine without the moral failure. This is fellow-feeling across the divine-human boundary — the incarnate Son genuinely sharing the human experience.

[PHASE-C] 3270-001 | G2787G kibōtos | Reg 34 (covenant)
Term type: Property term — the ark as mediating sign
DESC (B.5 confirmed): Reverential awe before the holy — the ark as the mediating sign that orients the inner person toward the presence and faithfulness of God

AV-VERIFY 3270-001 | Rev 11:19
AV: Rev 11:19 — "Then God's temple in heaven was opened, and the ark of his covenant was seen within his temple. There were flashes of lightning, rumblings, peals of thunder, an earthquake, and heavy hail."
DESC covers: The ark as mediating sign orienting toward God's presence; reverential awe named through the theophanic phenomena.
VERSE also shows: The ark is seen in the opened heavenly temple — the cosmic theophany (lightning, thunder, earthquake, hail) surrounding the moment of disclosure creates a context of overwhelming divine presence. The inner-being response is reverential awe before the holy. The group has 2 verses; the second likely reinforces this theophanic dimension.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Dependence / Creatureliness
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner orientation evoked by the ark's disclosure in a theophanic context is reverential awe before the holy — the creature's posture before overwhelming divine presence and faithfulness. This is Dependence/Creatureliness (the inner posture of the creature before God's holy majesty), not Moral Character (the automated label) and not Divine-Human Correspondence (though the divine presence is what generates the posture). The inner characteristic is the human stance of awe-dependent orientation. Correcting from Moral Character.

[PHASE-C] 3306-002 | H3748 ke.ri.tut | Reg 34 (covenant)

DESC covers: The metaphor of divorce for covenantal rupture — the rhetorical question implies there is no certificate; the separation is due to Israel's iniquity, not divine abandonment.
VERSE also shows: The verse is structured as a defence of God's faithfulness — the divorce metaphor is deployed to clarify that the separation was caused by Israel's transgressions. The inner-being content is Israel's apostasy as the ground of rupture, and God's implicit refusal to be the party who abandoned.

AV: Dan 9:24 — "Seventy weeks are decreed about your people and your holy city, to finish the transgression, to put an end to sin, and to atone for iniquity, to bring in everlasting righteousness, to seal both vision and prophet, and to anoint a most holy place."
DESC covers: The seventy weeks as the decreed period for ending sin, atonement, and the arrival of everlasting righteousness.
VERSE also shows: The six purposes (finish transgression, end sin, atone iniquity, bring everlasting righteousness, seal vision/prophet, anoint holy place) span both inner-being categories (sin, iniquity, righteousness) and eschatological/structural ones (vision, holy place). The description correctly focuses on the inner-being programme.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Transformation
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The divinely appointed programme for the inner-being completion of the person and community — sin ended, iniquity atoned, everlasting righteousness arrived. This is Transformation (the movement from sin/iniquity toward righteousness as the inner-being trajectory). The automated label Divine-Human Correspondence is not appropriate (the weeks are a programme, not a mirroring structure). Correcting to Transformation, HUMAN (the transformation is of the human community, accomplished through divine action).

[PHASE-C] 765-002 | H1285 be.rit | Reg 34 (covenant)
Term type: Characteristic term
DESC (confirmed): The Sinai/Mosaic covenant — bilateral covenant of law and obedience

AV-VERIFY 765-002 | Deu 7:9
AV: Deu 7:9 — "Know therefore that the Lord your God is God, the faithful God who keeps covenant and steadfast love with those who love him and keep his commandments, to a thousand generations."
DESC covers: The bilateral covenant — conditioned on love and commandment-keeping.
VERSE also shows: God's covenant-keeping is paired with steadfast love — faithfulness and love are inseparable in his inner character. The condition ("those who love him and keep his commandments") names the human inner-being obligations. The 76-verse corpus is the largest in Reg 34 and spans the entire Mosaic covenant corpus.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT — though the anchor verse actually shows God's side of the bilateral covenant with great emphasis. The 76-verse corpus will include both poles.
FLAG: MINOR — "bilateral" in the description is a structural description; the anchor verse emphasises the divine side. No correction needed.
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Volition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: NONE
NOTES: The bilateral covenant structure requires inner decisions on both sides — God's faithful commitment and the human's obedient response. The inner characteristic is the volitional commitment on both sides: love, obedience, commandment-keeping as acts of will. Volition is more precise than the automated label Relational Disposition, which misses the enacted-commitment dimension. Dominant-subject NONE — both divine and human sides are integral to the structure.

[SESSION-D] DIM-34-SD001
REGISTRY: 34 (covenant)
SESSION-TARGET: D
DESCRIPTION: The covenant vocabulary of Reg 34 spans at least four distinct dimension categories across the be.rit and ka.rat groups: Relational Disposition (unconditional divine commitment, relational bond), Transformation (new covenant, heart-writing), Volition (bilateral obligation, obedience-commitment), and Moral Character (oath-keeping, integrity). This multi-dimensional structure is not a grouping failure — it reflects the genuine inner-being complexity of covenant as a category that encompasses relational bond, inner transformation, volitional commitment, and moral integrity simultaneously. Session D should examine whether the covenant vocabulary of Reg 34 serves as a structural backbone for the other C17 registries: whether love (Reg 103), mercy (Reg 111), compassion (Reg 23) and peace (Reg 117) can be understood as facets of the single inner-being architecture that covenant names. The hypothesis is that covenant in Reg 34 is not merely one registry among equals in C17 but the structural container within which the other relational-disposition registries operate.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_session_research_flags insert

PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 6660

VERSE also shows: The curse falls on those who transgressed — the ritual's self-imprecatory logic is invoked: they cut the calf, agreeing to be cut if they broke the covenant; now God enacts that consequence. The transgression is the inner moral failure that the oath was designed to prevent.

DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN

[PHASE-C] 5367-001 | G2844 koinōnos | Reg 62 (fellowship)
Term type: Characteristic term — names the one who participates
DESC (confirmed): Term names the participant in a shared inner-spiritual reality — one who shares in divine nature, suffering, comfort, or cultic alignment through inner disposition and orientation

AV-VERIFY 5367-001 | 2Pe 1:4
AV: 2Pe 1:4 — "by which he has granted to us his precious and very great promises, so that through them you may become partakers of the divine nature, having escaped from the corruption that is in the world because of sinful desire."
DESC covers: Participant in a shared inner-spiritual reality — sharing in divine nature through the promises; escape from corruption as the negative pole.
VERSE also shows: The partaking of divine nature is the positive inner-being content; escape from corruption (sinful desire) is the negative condition left behind. The transformation from corruption-participant to divine-nature-participant is the inner movement. The "through them" (the promises) identifies the mechanism.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Divine-Human Correspondence
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner-being reality of participating in divine nature — the human person constituted as a sharer in what belongs to God. This is Divine-Human Correspondence: the characteristic is defined by the crossing of the divine-human boundary, with the human as the one who participates in what is originally divine. Automated label confirmed. DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN — it is the human person who becomes a partaker; the divine nature is the content shared.

[PHASE-C] 5367-002 | G2844 koinōnos | Reg 62 (fellowship)
Term type: Characteristic term
DESC (confirmed): Term names the participant in a moral or relational bond — one whose inner orientation places them in solidarity or complicity with another person or cause

AV-VERIFY 5367-002 | Mat 23:30
AV: Mat 23:30 — "saying, 'If we had lived in the days of our fathers, we would not have taken part with them in shedding the blood of the prophets.'"
DESC covers: Participant in a moral or relational bond — here solidarity or complicity through inner orientation.
VERSE also shows: The scribes and Pharisees claim they would not have been participants (koinōnoi) in their fathers' murders — but Jesus's argument (Mat 23:31) is that they thereby testify against themselves, showing they are indeed the sons of those who murdered. The koinōnos claim is being rejected even as it is made. The inner orientation of moral complicity versus moral separation is the inner-being content.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT — the verse grounds complicity/solidarity as an inner orientation, even in its disavowal.
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Moral Character
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner orientation that constitutes moral solidarity or complicity — whether one is inwardly aligned with a person or cause. Automated label Moral Character confirmed. The group captures koinōnos in its moral-character dimension: the inner quality of the person that constitutes them a participant in another's moral acts.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7247

[PHASE-C] 873-001 | G2842 koinōnia | Reg 62 (fellowship)
Term type: Characteristic term
DESC (confirmed): Term names the inner-relational orientation of shared life and communion with God — the spiritual participation in the divine nature, the Son, and the Spirit that constitutes the believer's vertical fellowship

AV-VERIFY 873-001 | Phili 3:10
AV: Phili 3:10 — "that I may know him and the power of his resurrection, and may share his sufferings, becoming like him in his death."
DESC covers: Spiritual participation — sharing in Christ's sufferings as the inner-relational orientation of vertical fellowship.
VERSE also shows: The fellowship of Christ's sufferings is not abstract — it is becoming like him in his death. The inner-being content is conformity to Christ through shared suffering, directed by the desire to know him. The participation is both relational (with Christ) and transforming (becoming like him).
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: MINOR — the anchor verse shows a transforming, suffering-participation dimension alongside the vertical fellowship. No correction needed; the description captures the vertical orientation.

AV-VERIFY 873-001 | 1Jo 1:3
AV: 1Jo 1:3 — "that which we have seen and heard we proclaim also to you, so that you too may have fellowship with us; and indeed our fellowship is with the Father and with his Son Jesus Christ."
DESC covers: Inner-relational orientation of communion with God — "our fellowship is with the Father and with his Son."
VERSE also shows: The fellowship is explicitly Trinitarian (Father and Son); the horizontal fellowship ("with us") is grounded in and flows from the vertical. The proclamation is itself the vehicle through which the fellowship is extended. With 8 verses the corpus spans vertical and probably horizontal fellowship.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Divine-Human Correspondence
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner-relational orientation of communion with the divine persons — the human person's participation in the shared life of the Father and Son. This is Divine-Human Correspondence: the defining feature of the group is that fellowship crosses the divine-human boundary; the human participates in what is intrinsically divine (the Father-Son relationship). The automated label Relational Disposition describes the toward-another quality correctly but misses the boundary-crossing nature that is constitutive of this group. The Phili 3:10 anchor shows participation in Christ's sufferings as a dimension of this same fellowship — the correspondence operates through suffering-solidarity as well as communion. Correcting from Relational Disposition to Divine-Human Correspondence.

[SESSION-D] DIM-62-SD001
REGISTRY: 62 (fellowship)
SESSION-TARGET: D
DESCRIPTION: Reg 62 (fellowship) has four groups that together trace three axes of koinōnia: (1) the divine-human correspondence axis (5367-001 — partaking of divine nature; 873-001 — communion with Father and Son), (2) the moral-character axis (5367-002 — solidarity/complicity), and (3) the horizontal-relational axis (873-002 — mutual belonging among believers). These three axes are not independent — the horizontal fellowship among believers (873-002) is explicitly grounded in the vertical fellowship with God (1Jo 1:3). Session D should examine whether the fellowship vocabulary of Reg 62 encodes a structural relationship: that genuine human inner-relational community (C17's relational-disposition cluster) is grounded in and derives from participation in the divine community (Father-Son-Spirit). This would make Reg 62 (fellowship) functionally analogous to Reg 34 (covenant) as a structural container: covenant names the bond, fellowship names the participatory inner reality of that bond.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_session_research_flags insert

PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7244

Genuine fellowship presupposes shared inner character (righteousness, light). The 6-verse corpus likely includes positive examples of shared life among believers alongside this negative framing.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT

[PHASE-C] 5377-001 | G0863H afiēmi | Reg 64 (forgiveness)
Term type: Property term — forgiveness as the act expressing the inner releasing
DESC (confirmed): Term names God's act of releasing a person from the guilt and penalty of sin — the vertical forgiveness that restores the inner standing of the person before God

AV-VERIFY 5377-001 | Luk 7:47
AV: Luk 7:47 — "Therefore I tell you, her sins, which are many, are forgiven — for she loved much. But he who is forgiven little, loves little."
DESC covers: God's act of releasing from guilt — "her sins are forgiven" is the vertical release named.
VERSE also shows: The verse establishes a reciprocal relationship between forgiveness and love: forgiven much → loves much; forgiven little → loves little. The inner-being consequence of divine forgiveness is the inner disposition of love. The forgiveness itself restores the inner standing and produces a new inner orientation.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: MINOR — the verse also shows the inner-being consequence of forgiveness (love produced). This is not a description gap; it is a Session B observation.
ACTION: None

[SESSION-B] DIM-64-001
REGISTRY: 64 (forgiveness)
DESCRIPTION: Luk 7:47 (anchor for group 5377-001) establishes an explicit inner-being grammar of forgiveness: the quantity of forgiveness received determines the intensity of the inner orientation of love produced — "she loved much because she was forgiven much; he who is forgiven little loves little." This is not merely a motivational claim but an inner-being causal chain: divine forgiveness (vertical release) → inner love-orientation (relational disposition). Session B for Reg 64 should examine whether this causal chain — forgiveness received → love orientation produced — is a recurring inner-being pattern across the forgiveness corpus, and how it relates to the grace-supplication chain already identified in Reg 68 (grace given → supplication produced, from DIM-068 Session C data). The hypothesis: forgiveness and grace both operate as inner-being generators that produce specific downstream inner orientations (love and supplication respectively).
PATCH-TARGET: wa_session_b_findings insert

DIMENSION: Relational Disposition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: GOD
NOTES: God's act of releasing the person from guilt — the vertical forgiveness that restores the inner standing and produces love. The automated label Divine-Human Correspondence is present, but Luk 7:47 does not show a mirroring structure; it shows a causal chain from divine act to human inner state. Correcting to Relational Disposition, GOD. The divine action is the dominant subject — it is God who forgives; the human love-response is the consequence, not a corresponding parallel.

[PHASE-C] 879-002 | G0859 afesis | Reg 64 (forgiveness)

[SESSION-D] DIM-64-SD001
REGISTRY: 64 (forgiveness)
SESSION-TARGET: D
DESCRIPTION: Group 879-002 (afesis — the unforgivable sin, Mar 3:29) defines the absolute limit of forgiveness. Session D should examine whether the forgiveness vocabulary of Reg 64 encodes a structural polarity: at one end, God's unconditional new-covenant forgiveness that remembers sin no more (5379-003, Jer 31:34); at the other end, the permanent condition of unforgiven guilt (879-002, Mar 3:29). Between these poles, the registry maps the full spectrum of forgiveness experience — cultic atonement, divine mercy, human horizontal forgiveness, intercessory plea. This polarity — absolute forgiveness / absolute non-forgiveness — may be a unique structural feature of the forgiveness vocabulary compared to the other C17 relational registries (compassion, mercy, love) which do not have an analogous absolute limit.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_session_research_flags insert

[PHASE-C] 880-001 | H5547 se.li.chah | Reg 64 (forgiveness)
Term type: Characteristic term

AV-VERIFY 880-001 | Psa 130:4
AV: Psa 130:4 — "But with you there is forgiveness, that you may be feared."
DESC covers: Forgiveness as a divine attribute that evokes reverential fear — "with you there is forgiveness, that you may be feared" is the precise statement.
VERSE also shows: The logic is counter-intuitive: forgiveness produces fear, not presumption. The inner-being consequence of God possessing forgiveness is not relaxed confidence but deeper reverential awe — the one who can forgive is the one whose power and holiness must be feared. The forgiveness makes the relationship possible precisely because it establishes the terms on which the awesome God can be approached.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

The automated label Emotion — Negative was flagged in Phase B as misassigned (likely triggered by "feared"). The inner characteristic is God's relational disposition of forgiveness, not the human emotional state of fear. Correcting to Relational Disposition, GOD. Note: the human inner-being response (reverential fear) is the consequence of the divine disposition, not the primary characteristic of the group.

## Phase C — Dimension Discernment: Reg 99 (kindness)

Session 8. Resuming from SESSION-END (Phase C complete through Reg 64). Phase C for Reg 99 — 28 groups.

Pointer sequences: Reg 99 Session B = DIM-99-001; Session D = DIM-99-SD001.

Confirmed Phase B descriptions in use:
  5737-001 researcher: "The covenant people as the object of divine care and human intercession — Moses's inner orientation of solidarity and advocacy for Israel grounded in God's steadfast love"
  5738-001 researcher: same
  5739-001 researcher: same
  5737-003 researcher: "The people as the object of God's liberating purpose — their situation as the ground of divine action, with Pharaoh's hardened refusal as the inner obstacle"
  5738-003 researcher: same
  5739-003 researcher: same
  5769-001 B.5: "Spiritual faintness and trust — the inner person in extremity, directing its cry and its trust toward God as the one who knows the way"

Observation noted from Phase B: H5971H, H5971I, H5971L are STEP multi-form variants producing near-identical groups; their -001, -002, -003 subgroups share descriptions and anchor verses. Dimension assignments for matching groups will be identical; each is still individually confirmed against its anchor verses.

[PHASE-C] 5729-001 | G5541 chrēsteuomai | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Characteristic term — verb naming the inner quality in action
DESC (confirmed): Kindness as inner quality of love — outward expression of love's inner character toward others

AV-VERIFY 5729-001 | 1Cor 13:4
AV: 1Cor 13:4 — "Love is patient and kind; love does not envy or boast; it is not arrogant."
DESC covers: Kindness as inner quality of love — "love is...kind" grounds kindness as an attribute of love's inner character.
VERSE also shows: The love-hymn lists kindness as one of love's intrinsic qualities alongside patience. Kindness is not an add-on to love but part of its defining inner character. The verb form (chrēsteuomai — to be kind, to show kindness) names the active expression of this inner quality.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Relational Disposition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: Kindness as the active expression of love's inner character toward others — a relational orientation expressed outwardly. Automated label Relational Disposition confirmed.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7660

[PHASE-C] 5730-001 | G5542 chrēstologia | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Characteristic term — compound naming flattering-speech as an inner disposition
DESC (confirmed): Deceptive inner disposition expressed as flattering speech — false kindness targeting the naive

AV-VERIFY 5730-001 | Rom 16:18
AV: Rom 16:18 — "For such persons do not serve our Lord Christ, but their own appetites, and by smooth talk and flattery they deceive the hearts of the naive."
DESC covers: Deceptive inner disposition expressed as flattering speech targeting the naive — "smooth talk and flattery...deceive the hearts of the naive" confirms.
VERSE also shows: The inner motivation is appetite-serving ("their own appetites"), not genuine kindness. The flattery is the instrument of deception; the inner disposition is self-serving. The target is the inner person ("hearts of the naive").
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Moral Character
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The deceptive inner disposition that produces flattering speech — self-serving appetite masquerading as kindness. This is a stable inner character disposition (Moral Character), not primarily a relational orientation toward another. The automated label Relational Disposition (ROOT_INFERRED) misses the moral-character dimension: the characteristic is the inner condition of deceptive self-interest. Correcting to Moral Character.

[PHASE-C] 5731-001 | H5973B me.im | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — preposition marking departure from relational presence
DESC (confirmed): Departure from relational presence expressing inner relational states — grief at loss, guilt, inner fear of separation

AV-VERIFY 5731-001 | Gen 44:29
AV: Gen 44:29 — "If you take this one also from me, and harm happens to him, you will bring down my gray hairs in evil to Sheol."
DESC covers: Departure from relational presence expressing grief at loss — Jacob's dread of losing Benjamin names the inner grief that makes departure unbearable.
VERSE also shows: The "from me" (me.im) is the linguistic hook — it is Jacob speaking about losing his son from his presence. The inner content is anticipatory grief, the weight of prior loss (Joseph), and the vulnerability of old age. The grey hairs going down to Sheol in grief names the totality of the inner devastation.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5731-001 | Gen 44:32
AV: Gen 44:32 — "For your servant became a pledge of safety for the boy to my father, saying, 'If I do not bring him back to you, then I shall bear the blame before my father all my life.'"
DESC covers: Guilt, inner fear of separation — Judah's pledge creates the inner burden of responsibility; failure to return Benjamin means bearing blame for life.
VERSE also shows: Judah's inner state is one of moral accountability — a self-imposed burden of guilt that would last a lifetime. The departure ("if he does not come back") triggers the guilt. The inner characteristic is the weight of pledged responsibility.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Emotion — Negative
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner states of grief, guilt, and fear of separation expressed in the context of departure from relational presence. The dominant characteristic across both anchors is the negative inner emotional experience triggered by or feared in departure. Automated label Emotion — Negative (KEYWORD_STRONG) confirmed. The preposition itself (me.im) is the property term; the inner-being characteristic is the emotional content it frames.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7683

[PHASE-C] 5732-001 | H5971K am | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — "the people" as communal subject of inner states
DESC (confirmed): Military force as communal subject of inner responses to battle — fear, courage, trust in God, inner orientation required at war

AV-VERIFY 5732-001 | Deu 20:1
AV: Deu 20:1 — "When you go out to war against your enemies, and see horses and chariots and an army larger than your own, you shall not be afraid of them, for the Lord your God is with you."
DESC covers: Military force as communal subject of inner response — fear (not be afraid) and the ground for courage (God's presence) both named.
VERSE also shows: The command "shall not be afraid" presupposes the inner tendency toward fear when facing a superior army. The counter to fear is theological: divine presence. The inner-being content is the required posture of trust against the natural inclination of fear.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5732-001 | Jos 8:1
AV: Jos 8:1 — "And the Lord said to Joshua, 'Do not fear and do not be dismayed. Take all the fighting men with you.'"
DESC covers: Inner orientation required at war — the double command (do not fear, do not be dismayed) names both inner states to be overcome.
VERSE also shows: The command against fear and dismay is the divine address to the inner person before military action. "Take all the fighting men" follows the inner command — the outer action is grounded in the inner reorientation.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Emotion — Negative
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: Fear and its overcoming as the communal inner response in the context of war. The inner-being characteristic is the emotional orientation of the military community — fear (its presence, its command against, its replacement by trust). Automated label Emotion — Negative confirmed.

[PHASE-C] 5733-001 | H5971B am | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — "the people" as communal subject
DESC (confirmed): Relational community of belonging — gathered to or cut off from one's people as inner belonging, covenant faithfulness, or moral transgression

AV-VERIFY 5733-001 | Gen 25:8
AV: Gen 25:8 — "Abraham breathed his last and died in a good old age, an old man and full of years, and was gathered to his people."
DESC covers: Gathered to one's people as inner belonging — "gathered to his people" names the inner-being dimension of death as communal belonging.
VERSE also shows: "A good old age, full of years" frames the gathering as a completion and return — Abraham's death is not rupture but inclusion. The inner dimension is the sense of relational completion: belonging to the community of the dead who preceded him.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5733-001 | Lev 17:10
AV: Lev 17:10 — "If any one of the house of Israel or of the strangers who sojourn among them eats any blood, I will set my face against that person who eats blood and will cut him off from among his people."
DESC covers: Cut off from one's people as moral transgression — the cutting off names both the inner consequence and the moral cause.
VERSE also shows: The divine action ("I will set my face against... cut him off") is the judicial response to a specific moral violation. The cutting off from the community is the inner-social consequence of transgression.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Relational Disposition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner-being dimension of communal belonging — the orientation of inclusion or exclusion from the covenant community. Automated label Volition misses the relational-orientation quality; this is about the inner belonging-bond, not primarily about choosing. Correcting to Relational Disposition.

[PHASE-C] 5735-001 | H5974 im | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — preposition "with" framing relational presence
DESC (confirmed): Relational presence of God or companions as context for inner experience — worship, petition, strengthening, or humbling

AV-VERIFY 5735-001 | Dan 2:18
AV: Dan 2:18 — "and told them to seek mercy from the God of heaven concerning this mystery, so that Daniel and his companions might not be destroyed with the rest of the wise men of Babylon."
DESC covers: Relational presence as context — the companions are with Daniel in seeking mercy; divine presence is what they seek. The "with" frames the communal petition.
VERSE also shows: The seeking of mercy is a communal inner act — Daniel and companions together. The inner characteristic is the urgent petition arising from threat of death, directed toward divine presence.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5735-001 | Dan 4:34
AV: Dan 4:34 — "At the end of the days I, Nebuchadnezzar, lifted my eyes to heaven, and my reason returned to me, and I blessed the Most High, and praised and honored him who lives forever."
DESC covers: Divine presence as the context for the return of inner faculties and the orientation of worship.
VERSE also shows: The restoration of reason ("my reason returned to me") follows the act of looking to heaven — divine presence is what restores the inner person. The progression is: humbling → looking to God → reason restored → worship. The "with" (divine presence) is the transforming context.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Dependence / Creatureliness
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The relational presence of God as the condition of the human creature's inner restoration, petition, and orientation toward God. Both anchors show the human person in extreme dependence — facing death (Dan 2) or restored from degradation (Dan 4) — with divine presence as the critical context. Dependence/Creatureliness more precisely captures the inner posture than the automated Relational Disposition, which misses the asymmetry: the human creature depends on divine presence for inner stability and function.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7684

[PHASE-C] 5737-001 | H5971H am | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — "the people" as communal subject
DESC (researcher confirmed): The covenant people as the object of divine care and human intercession — Moses's inner orientation of solidarity and advocacy for Israel grounded in God's steadfast love

AV-VERIFY 5737-001 | Num 11:29
AV: Num 11:29 — "But Moses said to him, 'Are you jealous for my sake? Would that all the Lord's people were prophets, that the Lord would put his Spirit on them!'"
DESC covers: Moses's inner orientation of solidarity and advocacy — his desire for the whole people to have the Spirit names his intercessory inner heart.
VERSE also shows: Moses refuses jealousy on his own behalf and expresses expansive desire for the people's spiritual empowerment. The inner characteristic is generosity of spirit and solidarity — the opposite of self-protective jealousy. His advocacy is for the people to share his own experience of the Spirit.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5737-001 | Num 14:19
AV: Num 14:19 — "Please pardon the iniquity of this people, according to the greatness of your steadfast love, just as you have forgiven this people, from Egypt until now."
DESC covers: Moses's inner orientation grounded in God's steadfast love — the intercession appeals explicitly to divine chesed.
VERSE also shows: The intercession is structured: appeal to divine character (steadfast love), historical precedent (forgiven before), present petition (pardon now). Moses's inner orientation is both theologically grounded and urgently personal — he is pleading for the people's survival.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Relational Disposition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: Moses's inner orientation of solidarity and advocacy for the covenant people — a relational disposition of generosity and intercession toward the community, grounded in theological conviction. The automated label Moral Character named only the community as moral category; the researcher-confirmed description refocuses on Moses's inner posture. Relational Disposition is the correct dimension: Moses's inner orientation is directed toward the people in solidarity and advocacy.

[SESSION-D] DIM-99-SD001
REGISTRY: 99 (kindness)
SESSION-TARGET: D
DESCRIPTION: The am-variant groups in Reg 99 (H5971H/I/L, each with three sub-groups) produce a large corpus (427 verses each for the -001 groups) where Moses's inner orientation of solidarity and advocacy appears as the primary inner-being content of the anchor verses. This raises a structural question: why are "people/am" terms placed in Reg 99 (kindness)? The intercessory solidarity of Moses (Num 14:19 — appealing to God's steadfast love on behalf of the people) may be the inner-being connection — Moses's advocacy for the people is itself an expression of kindness/solidarity as an inner orientation. Session D should examine whether the community-solidarity vocabulary of Reg 99 (the am-terms, the im.ma.di terms, the im-terms) encodes a dimension of kindness that is specifically communal and intercessory, rather than individual. The hypothesis: Reg 99 may contain a communal or social-solidarity sub-pattern that is distinct from the dyadic relational orientation of the love/compassion/mercy registries.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_session_research_flags insert

PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7673

[PHASE-C] 5737-002 | H5971H am | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term
DESC (confirmed): Corporate inner spiritual condition of the people — rebellion, fear, trust, shame, orientation toward God

AV-VERIFY 5737-002 | Num 14:9
AV: Num 14:9 — "Only do not rebel against the Lord. And do not fear the people of the land, for they are bread for us. Their protection is removed from them, and the Lord is with us; do not fear them."
DESC covers: Corporate inner spiritual condition — rebellion (do not rebel) and fear (do not fear) both named as inner states to be overcome.
VERSE also shows: The command against rebellion is the inner moral-volitional command; the command against fear is the inner emotional command. The corporate inner condition being addressed is disordered: the people are tempted toward both rebellion (against God) and fear (of enemies). Caleb and Joshua's counter-address names what the inner condition should be.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5737-002 | Num 14:11
AV: Num 14:11 — "And the Lord said to Moses, 'How long will this people despise me? And how long will they not believe in me, in spite of all the signs that I have done among them?'"
DESC covers: Corporate orientation toward God — despising and not believing name the inner spiritual condition.
VERSE also shows: God names two inner states: despising (contempt, relational rejection) and not believing (cognitive-volitional refusal of trust). Both are directed toward God. The corporate inner spiritual condition is one of persistent rejection despite evidence.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Moral Character
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The corporate inner spiritual condition of rebellion, unbelief, and despising — stable inner dispositions of the community that constitute its moral-spiritual character before God. Automated label Emotion — Negative is partially accurate (fear is present) but misses the dominant characteristic: the rebellion and unbelief are moral-character qualities, not merely emotional states. Correcting to Moral Character.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7674

[PHASE-C] 5769-001 | H2098 zu | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — particle directing to inner content
DESC (B.5 confirmed): Spiritual faintness and trust — the inner person in extremity, directing its cry and its trust toward God as the one who knows the way

AV-VERIFY 5769-001 | Psa 142:3
AV: Psa 142:3 — "When my spirit faints within me, you know my way! In the path where I walk they have hidden a trap for me."
DESC covers: Spiritual faintness — "my spirit faints within me" is the exact inner state named; trust — "you know my way" names the ground of appeal.
VERSE also shows: The faintness is internal and complete — the spirit itself gives way. Yet the address to God ("you know my way") sustains hope in the midst of extremity. The particle zu points to the moment of inner collapse in the first line.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5769-001 | Psa 143:8
AV: Psa 143:8 — "Let me hear in the morning of your steadfast love, for in you I trust. Make me know the way I should go, for to you I lift up my soul."
DESC covers: Trust — "in you I trust...to you I lift up my soul" names the inner orientation.
VERSE also shows: The morning-hearing of steadfast love is the anticipated inner restoration — the psalmist seeks to know the way (divine guidance) and lifts the soul upward. The particle zu in Psa 143 (context) again points to the inner state of dependence and orientation.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Dependence / Creatureliness
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: Spiritual faintness and trust in extremity — the inner person at the limit of its own resources, directing itself toward God. This is Dependence/Creatureliness: the creature at the end of itself, relying entirely on God's knowledge and love. Automated label Vitality/Existence is close (the fainting spirit touches on vitality/existence of the inner person) but Dependence/Creatureliness more precisely captures the creaturely posture of appeal and trust. Correcting from Vitality/Existence.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7671

[PHASE-C] 5771-001 | H2090 zoh | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — demonstrative particle
DESC (confirmed): Term frames inner reflection on meaning and worth of human experience — wisdom on joy, futility, divine gifting

AV-VERIFY 5771-001 | Ecc 2:24
AV: Ecc 2:24 — "There is nothing better for a person than that he should eat and drink and find enjoyment in his toil. This also, I saw, is from the hand of God."
DESC covers: Inner reflection on meaning — "this also, I saw, is from the hand of God" frames the Qoheleth reflection on the inner worth of enjoyment as divinely given.
VERSE also shows: The recognition "from the hand of God" reframes enjoyment as gift rather than achievement — an inner-being reorientation from grasping to receiving. The particle zoh points to the whole experience of eat/drink/enjoy as the object of this reflective verdict.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

AV-VERIFY 5771-001 | Ecc 5:19
AV: Ecc 5:19 — "Everyone also to whom God has given wealth and possessions and power to enjoy them, and to accept his lot and rejoice in his toil — this is the gift of God."
DESC covers: Wisdom on joy and divine gifting — the same pattern: God gives both the possessions and the capacity to enjoy them; "this is the gift" frames the inner reception.
VERSE also shows: The inner-being content is the capacity to accept and rejoice — an inner orientation of contentment and gratitude. Without the gift of this inner capacity, wealth is meaningless (the wider Qoheleth context). The particle zoh again points to the whole complex as the object of reflective assessment.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DIMENSION: Cognition
DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner act of reflective recognition — Qoheleth's wisdom-seeing that identifies enjoyment and acceptance as gifts of God. This is a cognitive inner act (recognising, seeing, knowing) directed toward the meaning of human experience. Automated label Emotion — Positive (KEYWORD_WEAK) misses the reflective-wisdom quality: the group is not primarily about positive inner feeling but about the inner act of seeing truly and accepting. Correcting to Cognition.
PATCH-TARGET: wa_dimension_index.id = 7669

VERSE also shows: The boast is total-person — might, power, residence, majesty. The inner pride has externalized completely into the royal claim. This is the moment immediately before Nebuchadnezzar's humbling (Dan 4:31).
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE

[PHASE-C] 5775-001 | H2097 zo | Reg 99 (kindness)
Term type: Property term — particle pointing to moral consequence
DESC (confirmed): Term directs attention to consequence of inner moral orientation — outcome of covenant faithfulness or spiritual infidelity

AV-VERIFY 5775-001 | Psa 132:12
AV: Psa 132:12 — "If your sons keep my covenant and my testimonies that I shall teach them, their sons also forever shall sit on your throne."
DESC covers: Consequence of covenant faithfulness — zo ("this/thus") points to the dynastic outcome of inner covenant-keeping.
VERSE also shows: The conditional structure (if they keep → then their sons) makes covenant faithfulness the inner-being cause and dynastic continuation the outer consequence. The inner orientation of faithful keeping is what is at stake.

AV-VERIFY 5775-001 | Hos 7:16
AV: Hos 7:16 — "They return, but not upward; they are like a treacherous bow; their princes shall fall by the sword because of the insolence of their tongue. This shall be their derision in the land of Egypt."
DESC covers: Outcome of spiritual infidelity — zo ("this") points to the consequence (derision) of the inner moral failure (insolence, treachery).
VERSE also shows: The inner moral failure is compound — treacherous, insolent, turning but not upward. The consequence (falling by the sword, derision) is the judicial outcome. The inner orientation of false return (returning but not to God) is what zo points to in its consequential framing.
VERDICT: FULL ALIGNMENT
FLAG: NONE
ACTION: None

DOMINANT-SUBJECT: HUMAN
NOTES: The inner moral orientation (faithfulness or infidelity) whose consequences are named — the particle points to the moral cause and its outcome. Moral Character is confirmed: the group is about stable inner dispositions (covenant-keeping vs. spiritual infidelity) and their consequences. Automated label Moral Character confirmed.
